<tr>
<td class="noprint" colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><img alt="" data-file-height="60" data-file-width="60" height="33" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/33px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/50px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Soccerball_current_event.svg/66px-Soccerball_current_event.svg.png 2x" width="33"/> <i><a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Valencia_CF_season" title="2016–17 Valencia CF season">Current season</a></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Valencia Club de Fútbol</b> (<small>Spanish: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[baˈlenθja ˈkluβ ðe ˈfuðβol]</a></span>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencian_language" title="Valencian language">Valencian</a>: <span lang="ca-valencia" xml:lang="ca-valencia"><i>València Club de Futbol</i></span> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Catalan" title="Help:IPA for Catalan">[vaˈlensia ˈklub de fubˈbɔl]</a></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> also known as <b>Valencia CF</b>, <b>Valencia</b> or <i><b>Los Che</b></i>) are a Spanish <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> <a href="/wiki/Football_team" title="Football team">club</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">Valencia</a>. They play in <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> and are one of the most successful and biggest clubs in <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Spain" title="Football in Spain">Spanish football</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_football_records" title="European football records">European football</a>. Valencia have won six La Liga titles, seven <a href="/wiki/Copa_del_Rey" title="Copa del Rey">Copa del Rey</a> trophies, two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fairs_Cup" title="Fairs Cup">Fairs Cups</a> (which was the predecessor to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a>), one UEFA Cup, one <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="UEFA Cup Winners' Cup">UEFA Cup Winners' Cup</a> and two <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Super_Cup" title="UEFA Super Cup">UEFA Super Cup</a>'s. They also reached two <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> finals in a row, losing to La Liga rivals <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> in <a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2000 UEFA Champions League Final">2000</a> and German club <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Penalty_shootout_(association_football)" title="Penalty shootout (association football)">penalties</a> after a 1–1 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Draw_(tie)" title="Draw (tie)">draw</a> in <a href="/wiki/2001_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2001 UEFA Champions League Final">2001</a>. Valencia were also members of the <a href="/wiki/G-14" title="G-14">G-14</a> group of leading <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> football clubs. In total, Valencia have reached seven major European finals, winning four of them.</p>
<p>Valencia were founded in 1919 and have played their home games at the 55,000-seater <a href="/wiki/Mestalla_Stadium" title="Mestalla Stadium">Mestalla</a> since 1923. They were due to move into the new 75,000-seater <a href="/wiki/Nou_Mestalla" title="Nou Mestalla">Nou Mestalla</a> in the north-west of the city in 2013, but the final move date has been postponed while the stadium is still being built. Valencia have a fierce rivalry with fellow <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencian</a> club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Villareal_CF" title="Villareal CF">Villarreal CF</a>, with whom they contest the <i>Derby de la Comunitat</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> The rivalry is further fueled by the fact that they are the two most successful clubs in the region. They also have a long-standing rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Levante_UD" title="Levante UD">Levante UD</a>, also located in the city of Valencia, and with two other clubs in the <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencian region</a>, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9rcules_CF" title="Hércules CF">Hércules CF</a> and <a href="/wiki/CD_Castell%C3%B3n" title="CD Castellón">CD Castellón</a>.</p>
<p>Valencia is the third-most supported football club in Spain, behind heavyweights Real Madrid and <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> It is also one of the biggest clubs in the world in terms of number of associates (registered paying supporters), with more than 50,000 season ticket holders and another 20,000+ season ticket holders on the waiting list, who can be accommodated in the new 75,000-seater stadium.</p>
<p>Over the years, the club has achieved a global reputation for their prolific youth academy, or <i>"<a href="/wiki/Cantera" title="Cantera">cantera</a></i>." Products of their academy include world-class talents such as <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Albiol" title="Raúl Albiol">Raúl Albiol</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Palop" title="Andrés Palop">Andrés Palop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_%C3%81ngel_Angulo" title="Miguel Ángel Angulo">Miguel Ángel Angulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Albelda" title="David Albelda">David Albelda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaizka_Mendieta" title="Gaizka Mendieta">Gaizka Mendieta</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Silva" title="David Silva">David Silva</a>. Current stars of the game to have graduated in recent years include <a href="/wiki/Isco" title="Isco">Isco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jordi_Alba" title="Jordi Alba">Jordi Alba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Bernat" title="Juan Bernat">Juan Bernat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paco_Alc%C3%A1cer" title="Paco Alcácer">Paco Alcácer</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Valencia_CF" title="History of Valencia CF">History of Valencia CF</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Valencia1927.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="389" data-file-width="747" height="115" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Valencia1927.JPG/220px-Valencia1927.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Valencia1927.JPG/330px-Valencia1927.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Valencia1927.JPG/440px-Valencia1927.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Valencia1927.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Valencia squad in 1927.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The club was established on 5 March 1919 and officially approved on 18 March 1919, with Octavio Augusto Milego Díaz as its first president; incidentally, the presidency was decided by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coin_toss" title="Coin toss">coin toss</a>. The club played its first competitive match away from home on 21 May 1919 against Valencia Gimnástico, and lost the match 1–0.</p>
<p>Valencia CF moved into the <a href="/wiki/Mestalla_Stadium" title="Mestalla Stadium">Mestalla Stadium</a> in 1923, having played its home matches at the Algirós ground since 7 December 1919. The first match at Mestalla pitted the home side against Castellón Castalia and ended a 0–0 draw. In another match the day after, Valencia won against the same opposition, 1–0. Valencia won the Regional Championship in 1923, and was eligible to play in the domestic <a href="/wiki/Copa_del_Rey" title="Copa del Rey">Copa del Rey</a> cup competition for the first time in its history.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emergence_as_a_giant_in_Spanish_football">Emergence as a giant in Spanish football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Emergence as a giant in Spanish football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Faas_Wilkes_(1961).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1847" data-file-width="1385" height="160" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Faas_Wilkes_%281961%29.jpg/120px-Faas_Wilkes_%281961%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Faas_Wilkes_%281961%29.jpg/180px-Faas_Wilkes_%281961%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Faas_Wilkes_%281961%29.jpg/240px-Faas_Wilkes_%281961%29.jpg 2x" width="120"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Faas_Wilkes_(1961).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Faas_Wilkes" title="Faas Wilkes">Faas Wilkes</a>, the first foreigner ever to play for Valencia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a> halted the progress of the Valencia team until 1941, when it won the Copa del Rey, beating <a href="/wiki/RCD_Espanyol" title="RCD Espanyol">Espanyol</a> in the final. In the 1941–42 season, the club won its first Spanish <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">La Liga</a> championship title, although winning the Copa del Rey was more reputable than the championship at that time. The club maintained its consistency to capture the league title again in the 1943–44 season, as well as the 1946–47 league edition.</p>
<p>In the 1950s, the club failed to emulate the success of the 1940s, even though it grew as a club. A restructuring of Mestalla resulted in an increase in spectator capacity to 45,000, while the club had a number of Spanish and foreign stars. Players such as <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spanish international</a> <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Puchades" title="Antonio Puchades">Antonio Puchades</a> and <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> forward <a href="/wiki/Faas_Wilkes" title="Faas Wilkes">Faas Wilkes</a> graced the pitch at Mestalla. In the 1952–53 season, the club finished as runners-up in La Liga behind <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. In the following season, the club won its third Copa del Rey, then known as the Copa del Generalísimo. Valencia beat holders Barça 3–0 in the final in front of over 110,000 spectators at the <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Chamart%C3%ADn" title="Estadio Chamartín">Estadio Chamartín</a>, then the home ground of <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a>. The 1950s also saw the retirement of club greats like Salvador Monzó, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Asensi" title="Vicente Asensi">Vicente Asensi</a>, Amadeo Ibáñez, Antonio Puchades and <a href="/wiki/Pasieguito" title="Pasieguito">Pasieguito</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_successes">European successes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: European successes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kempes_en_Valencia.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="451" data-file-width="340" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Kempes_en_Valencia.JPG/150px-Kempes_en_Valencia.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Kempes_en_Valencia.JPG/225px-Kempes_en_Valencia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Kempes_en_Valencia.JPG/300px-Kempes_en_Valencia.JPG 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kempes_en_Valencia.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Argentine forward <a href="/wiki/Mario_Kempes" title="Mario Kempes">Mario Kempes</a> in 1979. He played 8 years for the club, becoming topscorer in two seasons.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>While managing indifferent league form in the early 1960s, the club had its first European success in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Inter-Cities_Fairs_Cup" title="Inter-Cities Fairs Cup">Inter-Cities Fairs Cup</a> (the forerunner to the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a>). In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inter-Cities_Fairs_Cup_1961-62" title="Inter-Cities Fairs Cup 1961-62">1961–62 season</a>, Valencia beat Barcelona in the final. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inter-Cities_Fairs_Cup_1962-63" title="Inter-Cities Fairs Cup 1962-63">1962–63 edition</a> of the Inter-Cities Fairs Cup final pitted Valencia against <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatian</a> club <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NK_Dinamo_Zagreb" title="NK Dinamo Zagreb">Dinamo Zagreb</a>, which the Valencians also won. Valencia was again present in the Inter-Cities Fairs Cup final in the 1963–64 season, but was defeated 2–1 by <a href="/wiki/Real_Zaragoza" title="Real Zaragoza">Real Zaragoza</a>.</p>
<p>Former two-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Footballer_of_the_Year" title="European Footballer of the Year">European Footballer of the Year</a> award winner <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano" title="Alfredo Di Stéfano">Alfredo Di Stéfano</a> was hired as coach in 1970, and immediately inspired his new club to their fourth La Liga championship and first since 1947. This secured Valencia its first qualification for the prestigious <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">European Cup</a>, contested by the various European domestic champions. Valencia reached the third round of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Cup_1971%E2%80%9372" title="European Cup 1971–72">1971–72 competition</a> before losing both legs to <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungarian</a> champions <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Ajpest_FC" title="Újpest FC">Újpesti Dózsa</a>. In 1972, the club also finished runners-up both in La Liga and the domestic cup, losing to Real Madrid and <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a>, respectively. The most notable players of the 1970s era include <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austrian</a> midfielder <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Jara" title="Kurt Jara">Kurt Jara</a>, forward <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Rep" title="Johnny Rep">Johnny Rep</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, West German midfielder <a href="/wiki/Rainer_Bonhof" title="Rainer Bonhof">Rainer Bonhof</a> and <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentinian</a> forward <a href="/wiki/Mario_Kempes" title="Mario Kempes">Mario Kempes</a>, who became the <a href="/wiki/Pichichi_Trophy" title="Pichichi Trophy">La Liga topscorer</a> for two consecutive seasons in 1976–77 and 1977–78. Valencia would go on to win the Copa del Rey again in the 1978–79 season, and also capture the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Cup_Winners%27_Cup" title="European Cup Winners' Cup">European Cup Winners' Cup</a> the next season, after beating English club <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> in the final, with Kempes spearheading Valencia's success in Europe.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stagnation">Stagnation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Stagnation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1982, the club appointed <a href="/wiki/Miljan_Miljani%C4%87" title="Miljan Miljanić">Miljan Miljanić</a> as coach. After a disappointing season, Valencia was in 17th place and faced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relegation" title="Relegation">relegation</a> with seven games left to play. Koldo Aguirre replaced Miljanić as coach, with Valencia just barely avoiding relegation, relying on favourable results from other teams to ensure their own survival. In the <a href="/wiki/1983%E2%80%9384_La_Liga" title="1983–84 La Liga">1983–84</a> and <a href="/wiki/1984%E2%80%9385_La_Liga" title="1984–85 La Liga">1984–85 seasons</a>, the club was heavily in debt under the presidency of Vicente Tormo. The club finally hit rock bottom when it was <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">relegated</a> at the end of the <a href="/wiki/1985%E2%80%9386_La_Liga" title="1985–86 La Liga">1985–86 season</a> and riven with internal problems, such as unpaid player and staff wages and poor morale. The club was relegated for the first time after 55 years in Spanish top-flight football.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andoni_Zubizarreta.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="280" data-file-width="248" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Andoni_Zubizarreta.jpg/130px-Andoni_Zubizarreta.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Andoni_Zubizarreta.jpg/195px-Andoni_Zubizarreta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Andoni_Zubizarreta.jpg 2x" width="130"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Andoni_Zubizarreta.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Andoni_Zubizarreta" title="Andoni Zubizarreta">Andoni Zubizarreta</a> finished his career with Valencia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Arturo Tuzón was named the new club president, and he helped steer Valencia back to La Liga. <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano" title="Alfredo Di Stéfano">Alfredo Di Stéfano</a> returned as coach in 1986 and Valencia won <a href="/wiki/Promotion_and_relegation" title="Promotion and relegation">promotion</a> again following the <a href="/wiki/1986%E2%80%9387_La_Liga" title="1986–87 La Liga">1986–87 season</a>. Di Stéfano stayed on as coach until the <a href="/wiki/1987%E2%80%9388_La_Liga" title="1987–88 La Liga">1987–88 season</a>, when the team finished 14th in La Liga. <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgarian</a> forward <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luboslav_Penev" title="Luboslav Penev">Luboslav Penev</a> joined the club in 1989, as Valencia aimed to consolidate their place in La Liga. <a href="/wiki/Guus_Hiddink" title="Guus Hiddink">Guus Hiddink</a> was appointed as head coach in the <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_La_Liga" title="1991–92 La Liga">1991–92 season</a>, and the club finished fourth in the league, also reaching the quarter-finals of the Copa del Rey. In 1992, Valencia CF officially became a Sporting Limited Company, and retained Hiddink as their coach until 1993.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazilian</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Alberto_Parreira" title="Carlos Alberto Parreira">Carlos Alberto Parreira</a>, fresh from winning the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 FIFA World Cup</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazilian national team</a>, became manager at Mestalla in 1994. Parreira immediately signed the Spanish goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Andoni_Zubizarreta" title="Andoni Zubizarreta">Andoni Zubizarreta</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> forward <a href="/wiki/Oleg_Salenko" title="Oleg Salenko">Oleg Salenko</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Predrag_Mijatovi%C4%87" title="Predrag Mijatović">Predrag Mijatović</a>, but failed to produce the results expected of him. He was replaced by new coach José Manuel Rielo. The club's earlier successes continued to elude it, although it was not short of top coaching staff like <a href="/wiki/Luis_Aragon%C3%A9s" title="Luis Aragonés">Luis Aragonés</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Valdano" title="Jorge Valdano">Jorge Valdano</a>, as well as foreign star forwards like Brazilian <a href="/wiki/Rom%C3%A1rio" title="Romário">Romário</a>, <a href="/wiki/Claudio_L%C3%B3pez_(footballer)" title="Claudio López (footballer)">Claudio López</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ariel_Ortega" title="Ariel Ortega">Ariel Ortega</a> from Argentina and <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Ilie" title="Adrian Ilie">Adrian Ilie</a> from Romania.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_2000s:_Return_to_the_top_of_Spanish_and_European_football">The 2000s: Return to the top of Spanish and European football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: The 2000s: Return to the top of Spanish and European football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Valencia began the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Valencia_CF_season" title="1999–2000 Valencia CF season">1999–2000 season</a> by winning another title, the <a href="/wiki/Supercopa_de_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Supercopa de España">Supercopa de España</a>, <a href="/wiki/1999_Supercopa_de_Espa%C3%B1a" title="1999 Supercopa de España">beating</a> <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. Valencia finished third in the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_La_Liga" title="1999–2000 La Liga">league</a>, four points behind champions <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_de_La_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Deportivo de La Coruña">Deportivo de La Coruña</a> and level on points with second-placed Barça. The team's biggest success, however, was in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a>; for the first time in its history, Valencia reached a <a href="/wiki/European_Champion_Clubs%27_Cup" title="European Champion Clubs' Cup">European Cup</a> final. However, in the <a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2000 UEFA Champions League Final">Final</a> in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> on 24 May 2000, Real Madrid beat <i>Los Che</i> 3–0.</p>
<p>It was also Claudio López's farewell, as he had agreed to sign for the Italian side <a href="/wiki/S.S._Lazio" title="S.S. Lazio">Lazio</a>, also leaving was <a href="/wiki/Javier_Farin%C3%B3s" title="Javier Farinós">Javier Farinós</a> for <a href="/wiki/Inter_Milan" title="Inter Milan">Internazionale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gerard_L%C3%B3pez" title="Gerard López">Gerard López</a> for Barcelona. The notable signings of that summer were <a href="/wiki/John_Carew" title="John Carew">John Carew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Baraja" title="Rubén Baraja">Rubén Baraja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Ayala" title="Roberto Ayala">Roberto Ayala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Vicente Rodríguez">Vicente Rodríguez</a> and Brazilian left back <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A1bio_Aur%C3%A9lio" title="Fábio Aurélio">Fábio Aurélio</a>. Also bought that season was <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Aimar" title="Pablo Aimar">Pablo Aimar</a> in January. Baraja, Aimar, Vicente and Ayala would soon become a staple of Valencia's dominance of the early 2000s in La Liga.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">

</div>
<div style="position:absolute; z-index:2; top:80%; left:73%; height: 0; width: 0; margin: 0; padding: 0;">
<div style="position:relative; text-align:center; left: -5em; top:-0.65em; width:10em; line-height:1.4em; white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Claudio_L%C3%B3pez_(footballer)" title="Claudio López (footballer)"><b>Claudio López</b></a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align:center; font-size:smaller"><a href="/wiki/2000_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2000 UEFA Champions League Final">2000 UEFA Champions League Final</a> starting lineup</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Valencia started the championship on the right foot and were top of the league after ten games. After the Christmas break, however, Valencia started to pay for the top demand that such an absorbing competition like the Champions League requires. After passing the two mini-league phases, <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_C%C3%BAper" title="Héctor Cúper">Héctor Cúper</a>'s team eliminated <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> in the quarter-finals and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leeds_United_A.F.C" title="Leeds United A.F.C">Leeds United</a> in the semi-finals, and got ready to face <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> in the final; Valencia had reached two European Cup finals in a row. This time, the final was played in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> at the <a href="/wiki/San_Siro" title="San Siro">San Siro</a> on 23 May. <a href="/wiki/Gaizka_Mendieta" title="Gaizka Mendieta">Gaizka Mendieta</a> gave Valencia the lead by scoring from the penalty spot right at the start of the match. Goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Ca%C3%B1izares" title="Santiago Cañizares">Santiago Cañizares</a> then stopped a penalty from <a href="/wiki/Mehmet_Scholl" title="Mehmet Scholl">Mehmet Scholl</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Effenberg" title="Stefan Effenberg">Stefan Effenberg</a> put Bayern level after the break thanks to another penalty. After extra time, it went to penalties, where a <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Pellegrino" title="Mauricio Pellegrino">Mauricio Pellegrino</a> miss gave Bayern Champions League glory and dealt Valencia a second-straight defeat in the final. Valencia went on to slip to fifth place in La Liga and out of Champions League competition for the 2001–02 season. The final game of the season meant Valencia only needed a draw at the <a href="/wiki/Camp_Nou" title="Camp Nou">Camp Nou</a> against Barcelona to seal Champions League qualification. <i>Los Che</i>, however, lost 3–2, with a last minute goal from <a href="/wiki/Rivaldo" title="Rivaldo">Rivaldo</a> resulting in Barcelona qualifying for the Champions League while Valencia missed out.</p>
<p>The president, D. Pedro Cortés, resigned due to personal reasons and left the club in July 2001, with the satisfaction of having won one Copa del Rey, one Supercopa de España and having been runners-up in two successive Champions League finals. D. Jaime Ortí replaced him as president and expressed his intention of maintaining the good form that had made the club so admired on the European circuit. There were also some changes in the team and staff. <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez" title="Rafael Benítez">Rafael Benítez</a>, after helping <a href="/wiki/CD_Tenerife" title="CD Tenerife">Tenerife</a> to promotion to La Liga from the <a href="/wiki/Segunda_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Segunda División">Segunda División</a>, replaced Héctor Cúper after the latter became the new coach at Internazionale in Italy. Among the playing squad, Gaizka Mendieta, <a href="/wiki/Didier_Deschamps" title="Didier Deschamps">Didier Deschamps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luis_Milla" title="Luis Milla">Luis Milla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zlatko_Zahovi%C4%8D" title="Zlatko Zahovič">Zlatko Zahovič</a> left, while <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Marchena" title="Carlos Marchena">Carlos Marchena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mista_(footballer)" title="Mista (footballer)">Mista</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curro_Torres" title="Curro Torres">Curro Torres</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Rufete" title="Francisco Rufete">Francisco Rufete</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_de_los_Santos" title="Gonzalo de los Santos">Gonzalo de los Santos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Salva_Ballesta" title="Salva Ballesta">Salva Ballesta</a> all arrived.</p>
<p>From 1999 up until the end of the 2004 season, Valencia had one of their most successful periods in the club's history. With a total of two La Liga titles, one <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Cup</a>, one Copa del Rey, and one UEFA Super Cup in those six years, no less than five first class titles and two Champions League finals had been achieved.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Roberto_Ayala_y_Javier_Zanetti_-_07FEB2007_-_Francia_-_presidencia-govar.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="647" data-file-width="489" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Roberto_Ayala_y_Javier_Zanetti_-_07FEB2007_-_Francia_-_presidencia-govar.jpg/160px-Roberto_Ayala_y_Javier_Zanetti_-_07FEB2007_-_Francia_-_presidencia-govar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Roberto_Ayala_y_Javier_Zanetti_-_07FEB2007_-_Francia_-_presidencia-govar.jpg/240px-Roberto_Ayala_y_Javier_Zanetti_-_07FEB2007_-_Francia_-_presidencia-govar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Roberto_Ayala_y_Javier_Zanetti_-_07FEB2007_-_Francia_-_presidencia-govar.jpg/320px-Roberto_Ayala_y_Javier_Zanetti_-_07FEB2007_-_Francia_-_presidencia-govar.jpg 2x" width="160"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Roberto_Ayala_y_Javier_Zanetti_-_07FEB2007_-_Francia_-_presidencia-govar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
During Valencia's dominance of the early 2000s, Argentine <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Ayala" title="Roberto Ayala">Roberto Ayala</a> was a key component in their defence.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/2001%E2%80%9302_Valencia_CF_season" title="2001–02 Valencia CF season">2001–02 season</a>, their first game against title rivals Real Madrid produced a significant and important victory. This was followed by a record of 11 games won consecutively, breaking the existing one set in the 1970–71 season, the season they had last won the La Liga title under <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano" title="Alfredo Di Stéfano">Alfredo Di Stéfano</a>.</p>
<p>After a defeat in <a href="/wiki/A_Coru%C3%B1a" title="A Coruña">A Coruña</a> against <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_de_La_Coru%C3%B1a" title="Deportivo de La Coruña">Deportivo</a> on 9 December 2001, the team had to win against <a href="/wiki/RCD_Espanyol" title="RCD Espanyol">Espanyol</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Estadi_Ol%C3%ADmpic_Llu%C3%ADs_Companys" title="Estadi Olímpic Lluís Companys">Estadi Olímpic Lluís Companys</a> to prevent falling further behind the league leaders. Valencia were 2–0 down at half time, but a comeback in the second-half saw Valencia win 2–3.</p>
<p>In the second part of the season, Benítez's team suffered a small setback after losing 1–0 at the <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Bernab%C3%A9u_Stadium" title="Santiago Bernabéu Stadium">Santiago Bernabéu</a> to Real Madrid, but they recovered and achieved four victories and two draws in the following six games against <a href="/wiki/UD_Las_Palmas" title="UD Las Palmas">Las Palmas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athletic_Bilbao" title="Athletic Bilbao">Athletic Bilbao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deportivo_Alav%C3%A9s" title="Deportivo Alavés">Deportivo Alavés</a>, <a href="/wiki/Real_Zaragoza" title="Real Zaragoza">Real Zaragoza</a> and Barça.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px">
<div style="position: relative;font-size:80%">
<p><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg"><img alt="Soccer Field Transparant.svg" data-file-height="684" data-file-width="452" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg/200px-Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg/300px-Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg/400px-Soccer_Field_Transparant.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a></p>

</div>

</div>
<div style="position:absolute; z-index:2; top:18%; left:73%; height: 0; width: 0; margin: 0; padding: 0;">

</div>

<div style="position:relative; text-align:center; left: -5em; top:-0.65em; width:10em; line-height:1.4em; white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Jocelyn_Angloma" title="Jocelyn Angloma"><b>Angloma</b></a></div>
</div>

<div style="text-align:center; font-size:smaller"><a href="/wiki/2001_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2001 UEFA Champions League Final">2001 UEFA Champions League Final</a> starting lineup</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In one of those crucial games that they would come up against Espanyol, Valencia were trailing 1–0 half-time and a man down after the dismissal of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Amadeo_Carboni&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Amadeo Carboni (page does not exist)">Amadeo Carboni</a>, but after two goals from Rubén Baraja, Valencia achieved a 2–1 victory. Furthermore, Real Madrid's defeat in <a href="/wiki/Anoeta" title="Anoeta">Anoeta</a> to <a href="/wiki/Real_Sociedad" title="Real Sociedad">Real Sociedad</a> left Valencia with a three-point lead at the top of the table.</p>
<p>The final game of the season was at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Rosaleda" title="La Rosaleda">La Rosaleda</a> to face <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_CF" title="Málaga CF">Málaga</a>, on 5 May 2002, a date that has since gone down in Valencia's history. The team shut itself away in <a href="/wiki/Benalm%C3%A1dena" title="Benalmádena">Benalmádena</a>, close to the scene of the game, in order to gain focus. An early goal from <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Ayala" title="Roberto Ayala">Roberto Ayala</a> and another close to half-time from Fábio Aurélio assured them their fifth La Liga title, 31 years after their last title win.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_Valencia_CF_season" title="2002–03 Valencia CF season">2002–03 season</a> was a disappointing one for Valencia, as they failed in their attempt to retain the Liga title and ended up outside of the Champions League spots in fifth, behind <a href="/wiki/Celta_de_Vigo" title="Celta de Vigo">Celta de Vigo</a>. They were also knocked out in the quarter-finals of the Champions League by Internazionale on away goals. The <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_Valencia_CF_season" title="2003–04 Valencia CF season">2003–04 season</a> saw <i>Los Che</i> trailing long-time leaders Real Madrid. In February, after 26 games played, Real Madrid were eight points clear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> However, the latter's form declined late in the season and they lost their last five games of the campaign, allowing Valencia to overtake them and win the title. The club added the UEFA Cup to this success. Valencia had now been La Liga champions twice in three seasons.</p>
<p>In the summer of 2004, coach Rafael Benítez decided to leave the club, stating he had had problems with the club president; he would soon become manager of <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>. He was replaced by former Valencia coach <a href="/wiki/Claudio_Ranieri" title="Claudio Ranieri">Claudio Ranieri</a>, who had recently been sacked by <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>. His second reign at the club was a disappointment, however, as Valencia harboured realistic hopes of retaining their La Liga crown but, by February, found themselves in seventh place. Valencia had also been knocked out of the Champions League group phase, with Ranieri being sacked promptly in February. The 2004–05 season ended with Valencia outside of the UEFA Cup spots.</p>
<p>In the summer of 2005, <a href="/wiki/Getafe_CF" title="Getafe CF">Getafe</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Quique_S%C3%A1nchez_Flores" title="Quique Sánchez Flores">Quique Sánchez Flores</a> was appointed as the new manager of Valencia and ended the season in third, which earned Valencia a spot in the Champions League after a season away from the competition. The <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_Valencia_CF_season" title="2006–07 Valencia CF season">2006–07 season</a> was a season with many difficulties, a season that began with realistic hopes of challenging for La Liga but was disrupted with a mounting list of injuries to key players and internal quarrelling between Flores and new Sporting Director Amedeo Carboni. Valencia ended the season in fourth place and were knocked out of the Champions League at the quarter-finals stage by Chelsea 3–2 on aggregate, after knocking out Italian champions Internazionale in the second round. In the summer of 2007, the internal fight between Flores and Carboni was settled with Carboni being replaced by Ángel Ruiz as the new Sporting Director of Valencia.</p>
<p>On 29 October 2007, the Valencia board of directors fired Flores after a string of disappointing performances and caretaker manager <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%93scar_Rub%C3%A9n_Fern%C3%A1ndez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Óscar Rubén Fernández (page does not exist)">Óscar Rubén Fernández</a> took over on a temporary basis until a full-time manager was found, rumoured to be either <a href="/wiki/Marcello_Lippi" title="Marcello Lippi">Marcello Lippi</a> or <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mourinho" title="José Mourinho">José Mourinho</a>. A day later, Dutch manager <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Koeman" title="Ronald Koeman">Ronald Koeman</a> announced he would be leaving <a href="/wiki/PSV_Eindhoven" title="PSV Eindhoven">PSV</a> to sign for Valencia. But there was still no improvement; in fact, Valencia even went on to drop to the 15th position in the league, just two points above the relegation zone. Although on 16 April 2008, Valencia lifted the Copa del Rey with a 3–1 victory over Getafe at the <a href="/wiki/Vicente_Calder%C3%B3n_Stadium" title="Vicente Calderón Stadium">Vicente Calderón Stadium</a>. This was the club's seventh Copa title. Five days later, one day after a devastating 5–1 league defeat in Bilbao, Valencia fired Koeman and replaced him with <a href="/wiki/Voro_(footballer)" title="Voro (footballer)">Voro</a>, who would guide Valencia as caretaker manager for the rest of the season. He went on to win the first game since the sacking of Koeman, beating <a href="/wiki/CA_Osasuna" title="CA Osasuna">Osasuna</a> 3–0 in his first game in charge. Voro would eventually drag Valencia from the relegation battle to a safe mid-table finish in tenth, finally ending a disastrous league campaign for <i>Los Che</i>.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manolo_Llorente.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="452" data-file-width="471" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Manolo_Llorente.jpg/180px-Manolo_Llorente.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Manolo_Llorente.jpg/270px-Manolo_Llorente.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Manolo_Llorente.jpg/360px-Manolo_Llorente.jpg 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manolo_Llorente.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
35th and former president of Valencia Manuel Llorente.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Highly-rated <a href="/wiki/Unai_Emery" title="Unai Emery">Unai Emery</a> was announced as the new manager of Valencia on 22 May 2008. The start of the young manager's career looked to be promising, with the club winning four out of its first five games, a surge that saw the team rise to the top position of the La Liga table. Despite looking impressive in Europe, <i>Los Che</i> then hit a poor run of form in the league that saw them dip as low as seventh in the standings. Amid the slump reports emerged of massive internal debt at the club, exceeding €400 million, with reports claiming the players had not been paid in weeks. The team's problems were compounded when they were knocked out of the UEFA Cup by <a href="/wiki/FC_Dynamo_Kyiv" title="FC Dynamo Kyiv">Dynamo Kyiv</a> on away goals. After a run where Valencia took only five points from ten games in La Liga, an announcement was made that the club had secured a loan that would cover the players' expenses until the end of the year. This announcement coincided with an upturn in form, and the club won six of its next eight games to surge back into the critical fourth place Champions' League spot. However, <i>Los Che</i> were then defeated by fourth place contenders <a href="/wiki/Atl%C3%A9tico_Madrid" title="Atlético Madrid">Atlético Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Villarreal_CF" title="Villarreal CF">Villarreal</a> in two of the last three games of the campaign, subsequently finishing sixth in the table and failing to qualify for next season's Champions League.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_2010s:_Debt_issues_and_stability">The 2010s: Debt issues and stability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The 2010s: Debt issues and stability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Unai_Emery_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="530" data-file-width="336" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Unai_Emery_2012.jpg/150px-Unai_Emery_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Unai_Emery_2012.jpg/225px-Unai_Emery_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Unai_Emery_2012.jpg/300px-Unai_Emery_2012.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Unai_Emery_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Basque <a href="/wiki/Unai_Emery" title="Unai Emery">Unai Emery</a>, managed Valencia from 2008 to 2012.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>No solution had yet been found to address the massive debt Valencia were faced with, and rumours persisted that top talents such as <a href="/wiki/David_Villa" title="David Villa">David Villa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Mata" title="Juan Mata">Juan Mata</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Silva" title="David Silva">David Silva</a> could leave the club to help resolve the huge debt. In the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Valencia_CF_season" title="2009–10 Valencia CF season">2009–10 season</a>, Valencia returned to the Champions League for the first time since the 2007–08 season, as they finished comfortably in third in the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_La_Liga" title="2009–10 La Liga">2009–10 La Liga</a>. However, in the summer of 2010, due to financial reasons, David Villa and David Silva were sold to Barcelona and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>, respectively, to reduce the club's massive debt. But, despite the loss of two of the club's most important players, the team was able to finish comfortably in third again in the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_La_Liga" title="2010–11 La Liga">2010–11 campaign</a> for the second season running, although they were eliminated from the Champions League by <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> side <a href="/wiki/FC_Schalke_04" title="FC Schalke 04">Schalke 04</a> in the Round of 16. In the summer of 2011, then-captain Juan Mata was sold to Chelsea to further help Valencia's precarious financial situation. It was announced by President Manuel Llorente that the club's debt had been decreased and that the work on the new stadium would restart as soon as possible, sometime in 2012. During the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Valencia_CF_season" title="2012–13 Valencia CF season">2012–13 season</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Valverde" title="Ernesto Valverde">Ernesto Valverde</a> was announced as the new manager but after failing to qualify for the Champions League, he stepped down and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_%C4%90uki%C4%87" title="Miroslav Đukić">Miroslav Đukić</a>. On 5 July 2013, Amadeo Salvo was named new president of the club. Almost a month after Salvo was named president, on 1 August 2013, Valencia sold star striker <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Soldado" title="Roberto Soldado">Roberto Soldado</a> to English club <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> for a reported fee of €30 million.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sale_of_Club_to_Peter_Lim">Sale of Club to Peter Lim</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Sale of Club to Peter Lim">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2014, Singapore businessman <a href="/wiki/Peter_Lim" title="Peter Lim">Peter Lim</a> was designated by the Fundación Valencia CF as the buyer of 70.4 percent of the shares owned by the club's foundation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> After months of negotiations between Lim and <a href="/wiki/Bankia" title="Bankia">Bankia</a> (the main creditor of the club), an agreement was reached in August 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-Cleanup" role="presentation">

<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mestalla_Stadium" title="Mestalla Stadium">Mestalla Stadium</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mestallapanoramic4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1242" data-file-width="2472" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mestallapanoramic4.jpg/250px-Mestallapanoramic4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mestallapanoramic4.jpg/375px-Mestallapanoramic4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Mestallapanoramic4.jpg/500px-Mestallapanoramic4.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mestallapanoramic4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mestalla panoramic</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Valencia played its first years at the Algirós stadium but moved to the <a href="/wiki/Mestalla_Stadium" title="Mestalla Stadium">Mestalla</a> in 1923. In the 1950s, Mestalla was restructured, which resulted in a capacity increase to 45,000 spectators. Today it holds 55,000 seats, making it the fifth largest stadium in Spain. It is also renowned for its steep terracing and for being one of the most intimidating atmospheres in all of Europe to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 20 May 1923, the Mestalla pitch was inaugurated with a friendly match that brought Valencia CF and <a href="/wiki/Levante_UD" title="Levante UD">Levante UD</a> face to face. It was the beginning of a new era that meant farewell to the old place, Algirós, which will always remain in the memories of the <a href="/wiki/Valencian" title="Valencian">Valencians</a> as first home of the club. A long history has taken place on the Mestalla field since its very beginning, when the Valencia team was not yet in the <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">Primera División</a>. Back then, this stadium could hold 17,000 spectators, and in that time the club started to show its potential in regional championships, which led the managers of that time to carry out the first alterations of Mestalla in 1927. The stadium's total capacity increased to 25,000 before it became severely damaged during the Civil War; Mestalla was used as a concentration camp and a junk warehouse. It would only keep its structure, since the rest was a lonely plot of land with no terraces and a stand broken during the war. Once the Valencian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitch_(sports)" title="Pitch (sports)">pitch</a> was renovated, Mestalla saw how the team managed to bring home their first title, the 1941 Cup. An overwhelming team was playing on the grass of the redesigned Valencian stadium in that decade, team that conquered three Liga titles and two Cups with the legendary "electric forwards" of Epi, Amadeo, Mundo, Asensi and <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Gorostiza" title="Guillermo Gorostiza">Guillermo Gorostiza</a>. Those years of sporting success also served as support to recover little by little the Mestalla ground.</p>
<p>During the 1950s, the Valencia ground experienced the deepest change in its whole history. That project resulted in a stadium with a capacity of 45,500 spectators. It was a dream that was destroyed by the <a href="/wiki/Flood" title="Flood">flood</a> that flooded Valencia in October 1957 after the overflowing of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turia_River" title="Turia River">Turia River</a>. Nevertheless, Mestalla not only returned to normality, but also some more improvements were added, like artificial light, which was inaugurated during the 1959 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fallas" title="Fallas">Fallas</a> festivities. This was the beginning of a new change for the Mestalla.</p>
<p>During the 1960s, the stadium kept the same appearance, whilst the <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban</a> view around it was quickly being transformed. Moreover, Mestalla held its first European matches. <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a> were the first foreign team to play against Valencia at Mestalla. They played on 15 September 1961 and it was the first clash of a golden age full of continental successes, during which Valencia won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fairs_Cup" title="Fairs Cup">Fairs Cup</a> in 1962 and 1963.</p>
<p>From 1969, the expression "<i>Anem a Mestalla</i>" ("Let's go to Mestalla"), so common among the supporters, began to fall into oblivion. The reason was the change of name that meant a big tribute that the club paid to his most symbolic president that lasted for a quarter of a century. <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Luis_Casanova_Giner&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Luis Casanova Giner (page does not exist)">Luis Casanova Giner</a> admitted that he was completely overwhelmed by such honour, and the president himself requested in 1994 that his name was again replaced by the name of Mestalla, as it happened.</p>
<p>In 1972, the head office of the club, located in the back of the numbered terraces, was inaugurated. It consisted of an office of <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> style with a worth mentioning trophy hall, which held the foundation flag of the club. In the summer of 1973 there was another new thing, the goal seats, which meant the elimination of fourteen rows of standing <a href="/wiki/Terrace_(stadium)" title="Terrace (stadium)">terraces</a> providing more comfort and an adjustment to the new times. Valencia's management started to consider the possibility of moving Mestalla from its present location to some land in the outskirts of the town, but finally the project was turned down and some years later.</p>
<p>Mestalla hosted the <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain national football team</a> for the first time in 1925. It was chosen the national team's group venue when Spain staged the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 FIFA World Cup</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and at the <a href="/wiki/1992_Summer_Olympics" title="1992 Summer Olympics">1992 Summer Olympics</a> held in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, all of Spain's matches up to the final were held at Mestalla, as they won Gold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> Mestalla has been the setting for important international matches, has held several Cup finals, has been the home of Levante, a venue for the Spanish national team and exile for <a href="/wiki/CD_Castell%C3%B3n" title="CD Castellón">Castellón</a> and <a href="/wiki/Real_Madrid_C.F." title="Real Madrid C.F.">Real Madrid</a> in Europe.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_stadium">New stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: New stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Nou_Mestalla" title="Nou Mestalla">Nou Mestalla</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maqueta_Nuevo_Mestalla.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Maqueta_Nuevo_Mestalla.jpg/220px-Maqueta_Nuevo_Mestalla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Maqueta_Nuevo_Mestalla.jpg/330px-Maqueta_Nuevo_Mestalla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Maqueta_Nuevo_Mestalla.jpg/440px-Maqueta_Nuevo_Mestalla.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maqueta_Nuevo_Mestalla.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Model of <a href="/wiki/Nou_Mestalla" title="Nou Mestalla">Nou Mestalla</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 2008–09 season was to have been the last season at the Mestalla, with the club moving to their new 75,000-seater stadium <a href="/wiki/Nou_Mestalla" title="Nou Mestalla">Nou Mestalla</a> in time for the 2009–10 season. However, due to the club being in financial crisis,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> work on the new stadium has since stopped.</p>
<p>On 12 December 2011, club president Manuel Llorente reached an agreement with Spanish banking conglomerate <a href="/wiki/Bankia" title="Bankia">Bankia</a>, which insured the financial security to resume work on the new stadium. It was estimated that the stadium would be completed in two years and in time for the 2014–15 season, though continued debt problems and the eventual stepping-down of Llorente in 2012 meant the fate of the new stadium was once again left up in the air as the club continued to look for ways to finance its completion.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On 13 November 2013, Valencia announced an updated redesign by Fenwick Iribarren Architects. The new design reduced the capacity to 61,500. It also reduced the underground car park and downsized the original design's full roof and elaborate façade. There were also redesigns of the interior decoration. No date was given for when construction would commence.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kit_and_colours">Kit and colours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Kit and colours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Originally, Valencia's kit was composed of white shirts, black shorts and socks of the same colour. Through the years, however, these colours have alternated between white and black. The away kit has been shades of orange in recent years while third alternate kits have featured colors from the club crest—yellow, blood orange and blue.</p>

<p>The team have also attracted smaller, local sponsors over the years. One example is <a href="/wiki/Lamiplast" title="Lamiplast">Lamiplast</a>, a Valencia-based furniture company.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_anthem">Club anthem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Club anthem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The club assigned D. Pablo Sánchez Torella who composed the music of Valencia's anthem, named the "<a href="/wiki/Pasodoble" title="Pasodoble">Pasodoble</a>". The hymn was written by Ramon Gimeno Gil in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencian_language" title="Valencian language">Valencian</a> variety of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalan_Language" title="Catalan Language">Catalan</a>. The anthem was premiered and had its official presentation at the 75th anniversary of the club on 21 September 1993.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bat_logo">Bat logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Bat logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:122px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Escudo_de_Valencia_2.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1100" data-file-width="1080" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Escudo_de_Valencia_2.svg/120px-Escudo_de_Valencia_2.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Escudo_de_Valencia_2.svg/180px-Escudo_de_Valencia_2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Escudo_de_Valencia_2.svg/240px-Escudo_de_Valencia_2.svg.png 2x" width="120"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Escudo_de_Valencia_2.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Coat of arms of the city of Valencia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Valencia and the Balearic Islands were conquered by King <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon" title="James I of Aragon">James I of Aragon</a> during the first half of the 13th century. After the conquest, the King gave them the status of independent kingdoms of whom he was also the king (but they were independent of Aragonese laws and institutions). The arms of Valencia show those of James I.</p>
<p>The unique crowned letters "L" besides the shield were granted by King <a href="/wiki/Peter_IV_of_Aragon" title="Peter IV of Aragon">Peter the Ceremonious</a>. The reason for the letters was that the city had been loyal twice to the King, hence twice a letter "L" and a crown for the king.</p>
<p>There are several possible explanations for the bat; one is that bats are simply quite common in the area. The second theory is that on 9 October 1238, when James I was about to enter the city, re-conquering it from the Moors, a bat landed on the top of his flag, and he interpreted it as a good sign. As he conquered the city, the bat was added to the arms.</p>
<p>In May 2013, <a href="/wiki/DC_Comics" title="DC Comics">DC Comics</a> started a legal case against the club, claiming that the bat image contravened its trademark of the bat image related to <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Batman</a>. The image, however, had been used on Valencia's logo since 1919, with Batman first published 20 years later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>

<p><b>LL.</b> = La Liga; <b>CdR</b> = Copa del Rey; <b>SC</b> = Supercopa de España; <b>UCL</b> = UEFA Champions League; <b>UCWC</b> = UEFA Cup Winners' Cup; <b>UEL</b> = UEFA Europa League; <b>UIC</b> = UEFA Intertoto Cup; <b>USC</b> = UEFA Super Cup</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallery">Gallery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Gallery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed" style="font-size:88%; line-height:130%">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 116px">
<div style="width: 116px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 114px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alejandro_Scopelli.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="368" data-file-width="191" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/cf/Alejandro_Scopelli.jpg/171px-Alejandro_Scopelli.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/cf/Alejandro_Scopelli.jpg 1.5x" width="114"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Scopelli" title="Alejandro Scopelli">Alejandro Scopelli</a>, the first foreigner to win a trophy with Valencia, the <a href="/wiki/1962%E2%80%9363_Inter-Cities_Fairs_Cup" title="1962–63 Inter-Cities Fairs Cup">1962 Fairs Cup</a>.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 189.33333333333px">
<div style="width: 189.33333333333px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 187.33333333333px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Distefano_eg_1958.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="392" data-file-width="334" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Distefano_eg_1958.jpg/281px-Distefano_eg_1958.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/07/Distefano_eg_1958.jpg 1.5x" width="188"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Alfredo_Di_St%C3%A9fano" title="Alfredo Di Stéfano">Alfredo Di Stéfano</a> had three successful spells as manager of the club.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 166.66666666667px">
<div style="width: 166.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 164.66666666667px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Claudio_Ranieri.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="680" data-file-width="510" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Claudio_Ranieri.jpg/247px-Claudio_Ranieri.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Claudio_Ranieri.jpg/371px-Claudio_Ranieri.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Claudio_Ranieri.jpg/495px-Claudio_Ranieri.jpg 2x" width="165"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Claudio_Ranieri" title="Claudio Ranieri">Claudio Ranieri</a> managed Valencia on two occasions with mixed success.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 148.66666666667px">
<div style="width: 148.66666666667px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 146.66666666667px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cuper_Hector.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="320" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Cuper_Hector.jpg/220px-Cuper_Hector.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2e/Cuper_Hector.jpg 1.5x" width="147"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_C%C3%BAper" title="Héctor Cúper">Héctor Cúper</a> tenure saw the club rise back to prominence in European football.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 158px">
<div style="width: 158px">
<div class="thumb" style="width: 156px;">
<div style="margin:0px auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2538" data-file-width="1800" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg/234px-Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg/351px-Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg/468px-Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez.jpg 2x" width="156"/></a></div>
</div>
<div class="gallerytext">
<p><a href="/wiki/Rafael_Ben%C3%ADtez" title="Rafael Benítez">Rafael Benítez</a>, Valencia's most successful manager, with two league titles and one UEFA Cup over the period of three years.</p>
</div>
</div>
</li>
</ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transfers">Transfers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Transfers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rodrigo_Moreno.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="395" data-file-width="335" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Rodrigo_Moreno.jpg/220px-Rodrigo_Moreno.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Rodrigo_Moreno.jpg/330px-Rodrigo_Moreno.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/27/Rodrigo_Moreno.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rodrigo_Moreno.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Academy:_Training_Centre_Foundation_Valencia_CF">The Academy: Training Centre Foundation Valencia CF</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: The Academy: Training Centre Foundation Valencia CF">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since May 2009, Valencia CF has had a training centre, this is the first multidisciplinary training center for a football club in Spain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="external text" href="http://formacion.valenciacf.com/" rel="nofollow">Training Centre Foundation Valencia CF "The Academy"</a> offers university education,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> classroom training, and online training related to sport and football soccer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Valencia CF is one of the few clubs in Spain that organises a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sport_Management" title="Sport Management">Sport Management</a> MBA, the <a class="external text" href="http://formacion.valenciacf.com/masters_intro.php" rel="nofollow">MBA in International Sport Management</a>, currently performs with <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Catholic_University_Saint_Vincent_Martyr" title="Valencia Catholic University Saint Vincent Martyr">Valencia Catholic University Saint Vincent Martyr</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the 90th anniversary of Valencia CF, The Academy opened with the University of Valencia the first university course that studied the history of a football club, Valencia CF is the first football club in Spain, object of study on college.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Motorsports_involvement">Motorsports involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Motorsports involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Valencia CF were also involved in motorsports such as <a href="/wiki/Formula_One" title="Formula One">Formula One</a>, <a href="/wiki/Super_GT" title="Super GT">Super GT</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MotoGP" title="MotoGP">MotoGP</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moto2" title="Moto2">Moto2</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moto3" title="Moto3">Moto3</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MotoGP" title="MotoGP">250cc</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Formula_Nippon" title="Formula Nippon">Formula Nippon</a>. Valencia CF was an official partner of <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Racing" title="Toyota Racing">Panasonic Toyota Racing</a> in 2003 until 2008 to commemorate Toyota as their shirt sponsor. Valencia CF also sponsored all Toyota-engined <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Formula_Nippon" title="Formula Nippon">Formula Nippon</a> teams and also <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> <a href="/wiki/Super_GT" title="Super GT">Super GT</a> teams in GT500 and GT300 cars. In 2009, Valencia CF became an official partner of former 250cc team Stop And Go Racing Team and later in 2014 Valencia CF also became official partner of <a href="/wiki/Aspar_Racing_Team" title="Aspar Racing Team">Aspar Racing Team</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MotoGP" title="MotoGP">MotoGP</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moto2" title="Moto2">Moto2</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moto3" title="Moto3">Moto3</a> classes, respectively.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="E-Sports_involvement">E-Sports involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_CF&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: E-Sports involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Valencia_club_de_f%C3%BAtbol_eSports&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Valencia club de fútbol eSports (page does not exist)">Valencia club de fútbol eSports</a></div>
<p>In June 2016, Valencia opened an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_sport" title="Electronic sport">E-Sports</a> division with presences in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hearthstone:_Heroes_of_WarCraft" title="Hearthstone: Heroes of WarCraft">Hearthstone: Heroes of WarCraft</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Rocket_League" title="Rocket League">Rocket League</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/League_of_Legends" title="League of Legends">League of Legends</a></i> - in the last case, they joined <a href="/wiki/Be%C5%9Fikta%C5%9F_J.K." title="Beşiktaş J.K.">Beşiktaş</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santos_FC" title="Santos FC">Santos</a>, <a href="/wiki/FC_Schalke_04" title="FC Schalke 04">Schalke</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_eSports" title="Paris Saint-Germain eSports">PSG</a> in acquiring <i>League</i> teams. They announced their <i>League</i> roster on July 13, composed mostly of Spanish players, including some with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_League_of_Legends_Championship_Series" title="European League of Legends Championship Series">European League of Legends Championship Series</a> (EU LCS) experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Winners</th>

<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
